Jeff Sessions, R-Ala., testifies on Capitol Hill\" width=\"580\" height=\"326\" data-mycapture-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/media/2017/03/27/USATODAY/USATODAY/636262470220843572-SESSIONS.JPG\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"AP ATTORNEY GENERAL RUSSIA PERJURY Q&A A FILE USA DC\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"326\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"580\" /><p>Sen. Jeff Sessions, R-Ala., testifies on Capitol Hill in Washington at his confirmation hearing for attorney general before the Senate Judiciary Committee in Washington, D.C., Jan. 10, 2017.<meta itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\" content=\"Alex Brandon, AP\" />&nbsp;<span class=\"credit\">(Photo: Alex Brandon, AP)</span></p></aside><div class=\"clearfix\"></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>WASHINGTON, D.C. \u2014 Bremerton City Councilwoman Leslie Daugs, arrested in January on a\u00a0charge of \u201cdisrupting Congress,\u201d <a href=\"http://bit.ly/2nb2tan\">has been offered a plea deal</a> by federal prosecutors in the nation's capital.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The\u00a0deal would allow dismissal of the criminal charge\u00a0if she performs 32 hours of community service in Washington state.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>But Daugs isn\u2019t taking it.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1OW1DP2DW0\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"blog-oembed-wrap \"><div\n        class=\"js-oembed blog-oembed blog-oembed-usa-today blog-oembed-type-link\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"link\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"usa-today\"><style>\n    .oembed-asset-link { border-bottom: 1px solid #e1e1e1; }\n    .oembed-link-anchor { display: block; clear: both; }\n    p.oembed-link-desc { font-size: 100%; color: #666; font-weight: normal; margin: 0 14px 14px 14px; font-family: 'Futura Today Light'; text-align: left; line-height: 120%; }\n</style><div class=\"oembed-asset oembed-asset-link oembed-asset-usa-today oembed-simple-link-container\"><a href=\"http://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2017/02/02/washington-state-councilwoman-arrested-outburst-sessions-hearing/97386002/\" data-track-label=\"newrecircinline\" class=\"oembed-simple-link oembed-link-anchor\"><p class=\"oembed-link-desc\">Washington State councilwoman arrested for outburst at Sessions hearing</p><div style=\"clear: both;\"></div></a></div></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cI\u2019m going to fight this,\u201d Daugs said Monday following her arraignment at the H. Carl Moultrie Courthouse in Washington, D.C. \u201cI feel very optimistic.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div class=\"partner-placement partner-spike\"></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Daugs was arrested by\u00a0Capitol Police\u00a0Jan. 31 during Senate confirmation hearings for then-Sen. Jeff Sessions of Alabama, now the country\u2019s attorney general. Daugs said,\u00a0\u201cThis is bull****,\u201d in response to two men who she said were being disruptive by \u201chigh-fiving and fist-bumping\u201d in support of Sessions. She was escorted out of the hearing and\u00a0arrested before being\u00a0released the same day.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201c(Daug\u2019s) behavior disrupted and interfered with the Senate proceedings and the orderly conduct of business,\u201d Metropolitan Police Officer Eric Jeter wrote in the report of her arrest.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1OW1DPocII\" class=\"story-asset image-asset\"><aside itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" class=\"wide single-photo\"><img itemprop=\"url\" src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/05068cbe685dd4faf15cfb737e5a293b48d0de90/c=136-0-1108-549&amp;r=x329&amp;c=580x326/local/-/media/2017/03/27/Kitsap/Kitsap/636262207489517269-Screen-Shot-2017-03-24-at-4.01.47-PM.jpg\" alt=\"The police report chronicling Leslie Daugs&#39; January\" width=\"580\" height=\"326\" data-mycapture-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/media/2017/03/27/Kitsap/Kitsap/636262207489517269-Screen-Shot-2017-03-24-at-4.01.47-PM.jpg\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"Police report\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"326\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"580\" /><p>The police report chronicling Leslie Daugs&#39; January arrest in Washington, D.C.<meta itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\" content=\"Contributed photo\" />&nbsp;<span class=\"credit\">(Photo: Contributed photo)</span></p></aside><div class=\"clearfix\"></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Daugs disagrees that Sessions\u2019 hearing was disrupted by her actions and questions why the behavior of the two men\u00a0went unnoticed by police.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cI don\u2019t feel I disrupted Congress,\u201d she said. \u201cNothing in that room stopped.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The deal offered by prosecutors also would require Daugs to avoid being arrested again in the next four months, take a drug test and stay away from the U.S. Capitol. But Monday, she rejected that offer.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cLeslie believes it is worth the risk,\u201d her attorney, Mark Goldstone, said in an email.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The maximum penalty for the misdemeanor is up to six months in jail and a $500 fine. Daugs\u2019 next court date is set for June. She noted her attorney also will be filing motions to dismiss the case on various grounds as well.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>It is illegal\u00a0\"to utter loud, threatening, or abusive language, or to engage in any disorderly or disruptive conduct\" on the grounds of the Capitol. Daugs, along with three others,\u00a0was arrested during the Judiciary Committee's hearing at the Dirksen Senate Office Building.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1OW1DQB6vI\" class=\"story-asset image-asset\"><aside itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" class=\"single-photo float\"><img itemprop=\"url\" src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/4b0bc33e20fa2fde6d2525ea0619a2644d77fb9b/c=85-0-645-1000&amp;r=583&amp;c=0-0-580-1031/local/-/media/2017/02/01/Kitsap/Kitsap/636215754920791291-Portrait---LeslieDaugs-12.JPG\" alt=\"Leslie Daugs\" width=\"580\" height=\"1031\" data-mycapture-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/media/2017/02/01/Kitsap/Kitsap/636215754920791291-Portrait---LeslieDaugs-12.JPG\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"Leslie Daugs\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"1031\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"580\" /><p>Leslie Daugs<meta itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\" content=\"Contributed photo\" />&nbsp;<span class=\"credit\">(Photo: Contributed photo)</span></p></aside></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>News of her arrest\u00a0<a href=\"/story/news/local/2017/02/15/councilwomans-arraignment-dc-comment-set-late-march/97965272/http://www.kitsapsun.com/story/news/local/2017/02/15/councilwomans-arraignment-dc-comment-set-late-march/97965272/http://www.kitsapsun.com/story/news/local/2017/02/15/councilwomans-arraignment-dc-comment-set-late-march/97965272/\">has divided the Bremerton council</a>. Some members support\u00a0Daugs\u00a0and believe she is being singled out; others see it as a distraction that affects the reputation of the City Council.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Daugs, who\u00a0said she has\u00a0stepped up her political advocacy since\u00a0Donald Trump was elected president, had noted in an email to the City Council office before going to D.C. that \u201cyou never know if I might get arrested for protesting.\u201d She said the arrest was \u201cnot my finest hour\u201d but also believes she\u2019s speaking up, as a woman and a Filipino-American, \u201cfor those who do not have a voice.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Daugs was in D.C. in January with her husband, Daryl, who was attending meetings in his work as head of Habitat for Humanity of Kitsap County. She works as a security guard at Mountain View Middle School in East Bremerton and is the head of the local chapter of the\u00a0Service Employees International Union.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Daugs said Monday that she\u2019s been encouraged by supporters and plans to take the case to trial.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cI feel very positive moving forward,\u201d she said.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1OW1DR2C44\" class=\"story-asset gallery-asset\"><div class=\"card-film inactive\"></div><div "title": "Councilwoman who cried 'BS' during Sessions hearing will fight charge", "url": "http://rssfeeds.usatoday.com/~/285396792/0/usatoday-newstopstories~Councilwoman-who-cried-BS-during-Sessions-hearing-will-fight-charge/", "date": "03-27-2017", "source": "usa-today", "text": "Sen. Jeff Sessions, R-Ala., testifies on Capitol Hill in Washington at his confirmation hearing for attorney general before the Senate Judiciary Committee in Washington, D.C., Jan. 10, 2017. (Photo: Alex Brandon, AP)\n\nWASHINGTON, D.C. \u2014 Bremerton City Councilwoman Leslie Daugs, arrested in January on a charge of \u201cdisrupting Congress,\u201d has been offered a plea deal by federal prosecutors in the nation's capital.\n\nThe deal would allow dismissal of the criminal charge if she performs 32 hours of community service in Washington state.\n\nBut Daugs isn\u2019t taking it.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m going to fight this,\u201d Daugs said Monday following her arraignment at the H. Carl Moultrie Courthouse in Washington, D.C. \u201cI feel very optimistic.\u201d\n\nDaugs was arrested by Capitol Police Jan. 31 during Senate confirmation hearings for then-Sen. Jeff Sessions of Alabama, now the country\u2019s attorney general. Daugs said, \u201cThis is bull****,\u201d in response to two men who she said were being disruptive by \u201chigh-fiving and fist-bumping\u201d in support of Sessions. She was escorted out of the hearing and arrested before being released the same day.\n\n\u201c(Daug\u2019s) behavior disrupted and interfered with the Senate proceedings and the orderly conduct of business,\u201d Metropolitan Police Officer Eric Jeter wrote in the report of her arrest.\n\nThe police report chronicling Leslie Daugs' January arrest in Washington, D.C. (Photo: Contributed photo)\n\nDaugs disagrees that Sessions\u2019 hearing was disrupted by her actions and questions why the behavior of the two men went unnoticed by police.\n\n\u201cI don\u2019t feel I disrupted Congress,\u201d she said. \u201cNothing in that room stopped.\u201d\n\nThe deal offered by prosecutors also would require Daugs to avoid being arrested again in the next four months, take a drug test and stay away from the U.S. Capitol. But Monday, she rejected that offer.\n\n\u201cLeslie believes it is worth the risk,\u201d her attorney, Mark Goldstone, said in an email.\n\nThe maximum penalty for the misdemeanor is up to six months in jail and a $500 fine. Daugs\u2019 next court date is set for June. She noted her attorney also will be filing motions to dismiss the case on various grounds as well.\n\nIt is illegal \"to utter loud, threatening, or abusive language, or to engage in any disorderly or disruptive conduct\" on the grounds of the Capitol. Daugs, along with three others, was arrested during the Judiciary Committee's hearing at the Dirksen Senate Office Building.\n\nLeslie Daugs (Photo: Contributed photo)\n\nNews of her arrest has divided the Bremerton council. Some members support Daugs and believe she is being singled out; others see it as a distraction that affects the reputation of the City Council.\n\nDaugs, who said she has stepped up her political advocacy since Donald Trump was elected president, had noted in an email to the City Council office before going to D.C. that \u201cyou never know if I might get arrested for protesting.\u201d She said the arrest was \u201cnot my finest hour\u201d but also believes she\u2019s speaking up, as a woman and a Filipino-American, \u201cfor those who do not have a voice.\u201d\n\nDaugs was in D.C. in January with her husband, Daryl, who was attending meetings in his work as head of Habitat for Humanity of Kitsap County. She works as a security guard at Mountain View Middle School in East Bremerton and is the head of the local chapter of the Service Employees International Union.\n\nDaugs said Monday that she\u2019s been encouraged by supporters and plans to take the case to trial.\n\n\u201cI feel very positive moving forward,\u201d she said.\n\nRead or Share this story: http://usat.ly/2npaDh9", "images":
